<a id="s2"></a>
## §2. Verses by sub-group

All verses for cluster terms, grouped by the analytical sub-group the term belongs to. Within each sub-group the rows are sorted canonically (book · chapter · verse). The **Term** column shows the Strong's number and transliteration of the cluster term whose `wa_verse_records` row generated this entry; **Spans in verse** lists every term-span recorded at that verse location.

Status precedence: G = group-assigned (analysed) · SA = set-aside · NR = is_relevant=0 · P = pending in VC · UT = untouched (no VC row).

**ID columns:** `vr_id` is `wa_verse_records.id`; `mti_id` is `mti_terms.id` (also `wa_verse_records.mti_term_id` and `verse_context.mti_term_id`). Both are exposed so AI can author VCREVISE / VCNEW / VCVERSE patches directly from this report — no separate ID-resolver query needed. The `(vr_id, mti_id)` pair is the natural key for any `verse_context` operation.

## §3. Per-term comprehensive detail

Each term gets numbered sections: identity • meaning • anchor-verse linkages • groups • findings • pointers • auxiliary data. Verses are not repeated here — they are listed by sub-group in §2. Items linked only by registry are summarised here; exhaustive lists are in the appendix §4.

**Identity & meaning**

1. Strong's: `H7230` · Lang: Hebrew · Owner: OWNER

3. Sub-group: —
4. Term status: extracted · Evidential: — · Occurrences: 152

**Verses:** 41 distinct locations (see §2 for the verse table grouped by sub-group).

**Group memberships (1)**

| Group ID | Code | Description | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2213 | 1142-001 | Term names abundance or greatness applied to inner-moral realities — the weight or magnitude of iniquity, steadfast love, pride, or spiritual failure, shaping the inner relationship between the person and God |  |

**Findings — direct (Strong's mention) (0)**

(none)

**Findings — via anchor verse (2 unique)**

| Finding ID | Type | Matched anchor refs | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-062-T2-251 | OBSERVATION | Isa 47:9 | The occult-charming groups (H2267 — spell/charmer; Psa 58:5, Isa 47:9) involve the use of fellowship vocabulary in relation to non-human spiritual forces — charms are a form of joining with occult power. This is the nearest evidence of fellowship operating in relation to spiritual beings. OBS-062-024, OBS-062-035. |
| OBS-060-T2-064 | OBSERVATION | Neh 9:25 | The characteristic deepens memory in its covenantal mode: the accumulated record of divine giving across generations forms the memory-structure of Israel's inner-being identity. Each new giving adds to the memory of prior giving, deepening the narrative foundation of trust. Neh 9 (the long Levitical prayer) is itself a memory-act: reciting the history of divine giving as the basis of present covenantal renewal. Hos 2:15 invokes Exodus memory as the ground of eschatological hope — the memory of what God gave before shapes the expectation of what he will give again. The characteristic does not impair memory in any evidenced instance; it is constitutively tied to the faithfulness of remembered giving. |

**SD pointers — direct (1)**

| Pointer | Priority | Strong's ref | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| DIM-152-SD001 | MEDIUM | H7230 | rov (H7230, abundance) in the strife registry (group 1142-001) is assigned Divine-Human Correspondence because both anchors have GOD as subject (divine weariness of ritual; divine steadfast love) while related verses carry the human moral-failure pole. This raises a programme-level question: does the biblical vocabulary of magnitude (rov, rabah, and cognates) consistently operate in divine-human correspondence mode — the greatness of divine attributes set against and corresponding to the weight of human moral condition? Session D should examine this across all registries where magnitude vocabulary appears. |

**Identity & meaning**

1. Strong's: `G0019` · Lang: Greek · Owner: OWNER
2. Registry: R067 goodness · Legacy C-cluster: C10
3. Sub-group: —
4. Term status: extracted · Evidential: — · Occurrences: 17
5. Patch-authoring refs: `mti_id=885` · `md_version=2` · `vc_status=vc_completed`
6. Mounce short-def: goodness

**Verses:** 4 distinct locations (see §2 for the verse table grouped by sub-group).

**Group memberships (1)**

| Group ID | Code | Description | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1110 | 885-001 | Term names goodness as an inner-being disposition and Spirit-produced fruit — a quality that fills the person and is completed by God, expressed in righteous conduct and resolve |  |

**Findings — direct (Strong's mention) (14)**

| Finding ID | Type | Anchor verses | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-067-OBS-008 | OBSERVATION |  | G0019 Gal 5:22 glossed as "generosity" — semantic overlap with R65 noted |
| OBS-067-OBS-047 | OBSERVATION |  | G0019 and G5544 thin-evidence confirmed by small corpora; conclusions proportionally limited |
| OBS-067-T2-004 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Gen 1:31, Gal 5:22, Rom 3:12 | The evidence supports both, distinguished by term. Gen 1:31 (884-007) establishes goodness as pre-fall and pre-relational — the Creator pronounces creation "very good" before any human moral life begins. This is goodness as original created quality, not a response to fallenness. The agathōsunē coinage (G0019, 885-001), however, is pneumatologically concentrated — a Spirit-produced fruit listed in Gal 5:22. The Spirit-production context implies the fallen condition: the natural human condition is characterised by complete absence of goodness (Rom 3:12), so Spirit-produced goodness is explicitly a redemptive response. H2896A in 884-002 (human moral character) and 884-003 (experiential good) could reflect both original design (the human created to be and experience good) and the ongoing challenge of maintaining that orientation under fallen conditions. The registry carries both registers: goodness as created design (Gen 1 ontological goodness, doxological goodness of 884-001) and goodness as restored/Spirit-produced capacity (885-001, 886-002). (OBS-067-OBS-036, OBS-067-OBS-046, OBS-067-OBS-048) |
| OBS-067-T2-012 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Psa 34:8, Gal 5:22, Rom 11:22 | H2896A (tov): the primary Hebrew term is an adjective of extremely wide semantic range. At the definitional level, it names what is genuinely and concretely beneficial, pleasing, and right — a quality observable in persons, things, actions, words, and states. It does not begin with an abstract ethical definition; it begins with the quality of things that genuinely satisfy and benefit. G0019 (agathōsunē): a NT-era abstract noun derived from agathos (good). At the definitional level, it names goodness as a stable inner virtue — a characterological quality that the NT isolates from the broader agathos adjective to name as a specific inner-being phenomenon. G5544 (chrēstotēs): derived from chrēstos (useful, serviceable, good). At the definitional level it names a relational quality — the disposition of generous goodwill and kindness — that is the outward-facing expression of inner goodness. The three terms thus reveal, even before lexical analysis, that goodness operates at multiple registers: experiential-phenomenological (tov), characterological-virtuous (agathōsunē), and relational-dispositional (chrēstotēs). (OBS-067-OBS-007, OBS-067-OBS-008, OBS-067-OBS-009, OBS-067-OBS-088) |

The 42 XREF terms in R67's inventory flow to multiple registries, confirming that the tov and agatho/chresto root families are shared across a wide range of programme registries. | OBS-067-T2-129 | ETYMOLOGY | Psa 34:8, Psa 73:28, Gal 5:22, Rom 11:22 | H2896A (tov): root TOV with 10 sub-senses (SBF-067-Q088) — aesthetic pleasantness (1a), higher-nature pleasantness (1b), intellectual goodness (1h), gladness/well-being (1g), ethical rightness (1j). Conceptual origin is phenomenological: begins with concrete experience of what is agreeable and beneficial, rises to moral and covenantal categories. The root meaning reveals that goodness is not first an abstract ethical standard — it is first the quality of things that genuinely satisfy and benefit, recognisable in creation and in proximity to God. G0019 (agathōsunē): root AGATHOS — the classical Greek adjective for that which is functionally good/useful. The abstract noun suffix (-syne) creates a virtue-noun — naming goodness as a stable inner quality, not merely a predicate. The root reveals the NT's intentional move from adjective (applied to many things) to abstract virtue (naming a specific inner characteristic). G5544 (chrēstotēs): root CHRĒSTOS — serviceable, useful, good in a relational-functional sense. The root reveals a relational quality: what is useful and generous toward another. The NT elevates this from horizontal utility (serviceable) to vertical character (Spirit-produced generosity of disposition). (OBS-067-OBS-007, OBS-067-OBS-008, OBS-067-OBS-009, SBF-067-Q088) |
| OBS-067-T2-130 | ETYMOLOGY | Psa 119:68, Gal 5:22 | H2896A (tov) operates primarily as an adjective — modifying persons, things, words, actions, and states. Its adjectival nature means it names a quality of its subject rather than an action performed. However, H2895 (tov verbal — be pleasing) shows the root also generates a stative verb — describing the state of being good/pleasing. The grammatical range (adjective + stative verb + verbal noun in related forms) reveals that goodness in Hebrew is primarily characterological (it names what something is) and secondarily experiential (it names the state of being good/pleasing to someone). G0019 (agathōsunē) is exclusively an abstract noun — naming goodness as a substantive virtue. G5544 (chrēstotēs) is also exclusively an abstract noun. The NT's grammatical form (abstract nouns only) reveals a shift from the Hebrew's adjectival breadth (goodness applied across contexts) to a specialised inner-being virtue-noun. (OBS-067-OBS-007, OBS-067-OBS-008, SBF-067-Q088) |
| OBS-067-T2-131 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Gen 1:31, Psa 34:8, Gal 5:22 | H2896A (tov) has the widest semantic range of any OWNER term in this registry: aesthetic pleasantness, moral rightness, covenantal reliability, comparative excellence, experiential benefit, evaluative good, ontological goodness (Gen 1 creation pronouncement), volitional preference, and inner well-being. The 12 distinct modes identified at Q&A-022 correspond to 12 distinct positions within this range. The breadth is confirmed by the 10 sub-senses of the TOV root and the 9 distinct H2896A groups. G0019 (agathōsunē): narrow range — goodness as Spirit-produced inner virtue/resolve (4 NT occurrences, all Pauline, all pneumatological). G5544 (chrēstotēs): medium range — kindness/goodness/gentleness as inner character quality and divine attribute (7 occurrences). The semantic range across the three OWNER terms covers breadth (H2896A's 12 modes) and precision (G0019 and G5544's specialised NT meanings). (OBS-067-OBS-007, OBS-067-OBS-008, OBS-067-OBS-009, OBS-067-OBS-048) |
| OBS-067-T2-132 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Gal 5:22, Rom 11:22 | Yes — the programme's XREF architecture structurally encodes the disposition/act distinction: G0019 (agathōsunē — goodness as inner disposition, R67 OWNER) vs G0015 (agathopoieo — to do good, R65 XREF). The disposition/act distinction is real and lexically supported. Received vs given: the same term chrēstotēs (G5544) names God's goodness given to humanity (886-001) and the Spirit-produced human goodness given to others (886-002) — the received/given distinction is not lexically marked but dimensionally assigned (Dimension 11 vs Dimension 05). Condition vs quality: H2896A's 884-009 (shalom-condition of inner well-being) is a condition; 884-002 (human moral character and conduct assessed as good) is a quality. The vocabulary distinguishes condition and quality within the same root. (OBS-067-OBS-017, OBS-067-OBS-090, SBF-067-Q090) |
| OBS-067-T2-136 | ETYMOLOGY | N/A | The LXX connection is not directly addressed in the anchor verses, but inferrable evidence is present (SBF-067-Q097). | OBS-067-T2-137 | ETYMOLOGY | Gal 5:22, Rom 15:14, 2Th 1:11 | G0019 (agathōsunē) is almost certainly a NT coinage — not attested in classical Greek or LXX (SBF-067-Q099). Its entire 4-verse NT corpus (Rom 15:14, Gal 5:22, Eph 5:9, 2Th 1:11) is Pauline and pneumatological. The coinage reveals: the NT needed a term for goodness as a named inner-being virtue distinct from the adjective agathos that applies broadly. Agathōsunē says: goodness is now a specific inner-being quality, not merely a predicate applied to things. The development from H2896A's ten-sub-sense breadth to agathōsunē's four-verse precision is pneumatological concentration: goodness in its fullest expression named as a Spirit-enabled virtue. The coinage represents the NT's sharpening of the concept from broad phenomenological range (Hebrew) to named Spirit-fruit virtue (NT). (OBS-067-OBS-009, SBF-067-Q099) |
| OBS-067-T2-138 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Gen 1:31, Psa 34:8, Gal 5:22, Rom 11:22 | The full vocabulary arc from TOV to agathōsunē to chrēstotēs reveals a three-stage development: (1) H2896A (Hebrew breadth) — goodness as a pervasive quality covering the full range of what is genuinely beneficial, right, and satisfying: aesthetic, moral, covenantal, volitional, experiential, evaluative, and ontological. This is goodness at its maximum semantic reach. (2) G0019 (NT precision — inner virtue) — goodness concentrated into a named Spirit-produced virtue: a characterological inner quality of the Spirit-filled person. From 10 sub-senses to one named category. (3) G5544 (NT precision — relational disposition) — goodness concentrated into its relational-dispositional expression: the generous goodwill that characterises both God's stance toward humanity and the Spirit-produced stance of the believer toward others. The arc is: phenomenological breadth (Hebrew) → virtuous precision (NT abstract noun) → relational precision (NT dispositional noun). The complete semantic range encompasses all three stages — they are not replacements but cumulative layers of specification. (OBS-067-OBS-007, OBS-067-OBS-008, OBS-067-OBS-009, OBS-067-OBS-048, SBF-067-Q099) |
| SYN-INTER-067-028 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER |  | T6 confirmed that goodness has the most extensive vocabulary-sharing and cross-registry connection pattern of any characteristic analysed so far in the programme. T7 confirms through the vocabulary arc (Q&A-177) that this extensiveness is a lexical reality, not a programme classification artefact: the three root families (TOV, AGATHO, CHRESTO) each generate multiple terms distributed across multiple registries because the semantic ranges genuinely overlap. The vocabulary sharing (T6.4) is not the result of how the programme has drawn its boundaries — it reflects the actual lexical distribution of the Hebrew and Greek goodness vocabulary, which crosses conceptual boundaries that English vocabulary maintains more distinctly. The three-stage vocabulary arc (H2896A breadth → agathōsunē precision → chrēstotēs precision) tracks the same movement as the cross-registry distribution pattern: H2896A generates the widest distribution (TOV root to R103, to R42, to multiple other registries); the NT precision terms (G0019, G5544) generate narrower distributions (R65 and R99 respectively). As the vocabulary narrows to precision, the cross-registry connections narrow correspondingly. T6's structural pattern and T7's lexical arc describe the same underlying phenomenon: goodness vocabulary begins broad and specialises, and its cross-registry connections follow the same trajectory. |

Mic 6:8 defines this as doing justice, loving kindness, walking humbly — the equipped person has the capacity to live in right orientation toward God and others. Rom 15:14 names the goodness-filled person as one "able to instruct one another" — goodness equips for community. (3) Volitional alignment — to prefer and choose what is genuinely good (884-008). The volitional-preference idiom's 40 verses show goodness functioning as the criterion of the will's proper operation. The three purposes converge: the person equipped with goodness has the capacity to be good (character), do good (conduct), and choose good (volition). | OBS-067-T2-014 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Gal 5:22 | Goodness is primarily a quality — a settled characterological property of the inner being. H2896A functions predominantly as an adjective, naming what someone or something is. Agathōsunē as an abstract noun confirms this: it names the virtue, not the act. However, the registry's 12 distinct modes (OBS-067-OBS-048) reveal that goodness also operates as: a disposition (chrēstotēs — the inner orientation of generous goodwill, 886-001 and 886-002); a condition (884-009 — the inner well-being state, shalom-condition); and an evaluative act (884-007 — the divine pronouncement-of-good as a creative-constitutive act; 884-004 — the cognitive comparative assessment). The primary kind is quality, but goodness is one of the more multi-modal characteristics in the programme — it operates across quality, disposition, condition, and evaluative act depending on context and term. (OBS-067-OBS-048, OBS-067-OBS-016, OBS-067-OBS-017) |
| OBS-067-T2-015 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Gal 5:22 | Goodness is structurally complex — it has constituent elements at first encounter. DIM-67-001 (resolved via OBS-022, OBS-023, OBS-048) confirmed that the 12 modes of operation are genuinely distinct inner-being phenomena. The constituent elements at definitional level are: (1) the ontological pole — what God is in his being (divine goodness as character attribute); (2) the moral-character pole — what the human person is in their inner life (human goodness as quality); (3) the experiential pole — what is genuinely good for the person (goodness as the content of genuine satisfaction and benefit); (4) the volitional pole — what the person chooses and prefers (goodness as the criterion of the will). These four poles are constitutive of goodness as a category. They are unified theologically (all derive from and respond to God's goodness) but they are analytically distinct phenomena. (OBS-067-OBS-022, OBS-067-OBS-023, OBS-067-OBS-048) |
| OBS-067-T2-016 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Gal 5:22 | Best working description: Goodness is a characterological quality of the inner being — constitutionally located at the level of moral character and disposition — that engages moral evaluation, volition, and relational capacity simultaneously. It originates in God's own character and is received, expressed, and cultivated in the human person through encounter with divine goodness, Spirit-production, and volitional alignment with what is genuinely beneficial. Its impact on the person is threefold: it orients the will toward what is genuinely good (volitional alignment); it shapes the character to be and do good toward others (moral-relational formation); and it produces inner stability when rooted in nearness to God (experiential well-being). When absent, the person's will is misdirected, their moral assessment is inverted, and their inner stability is fragile. The registry description's formulation — "structurally beneficial... not just pleasing or approved but actually doing good in the deep sense" — accurately captures the ontological weight of the term. (OBS-067-OBS-001, OBS-067-OBS-029, OBS-067-OBS-048) |
| OBS-067-T2-019 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Gal 5:22 | From the data: Goodness is not merely pleasant or approved — the registry description explicitly names this. Tov's aesthetic sense (pleasant, beautiful) is part of its range but goodness-as-inner-characteristic is the moral-constitutive register, not the merely pleasing. Goodness is not merely outward action — the programme's structural decision to assign G0015 (agathopoieo — to do good) to R65 (generosity) and retain agathōsunē in R67 reflects this: the act of doing good is adjacent to but distinct from the inner quality of goodness. Goodness is not identical to love (R103), kindness (R99), or delight (R42), though it shares vocabulary and anchor verses with each. The precise boundary between goodness and love at Mic 6:8 ("to love kindness" — where love-of-kindness is listed as one expression of what is good), and between goodness and kindness (R99 shares G5544), requires Session D cross-registry boundary work. The data names the proximity but does not fully draw the line. (OBS-067-OBS-018, OBS-067-OBS-090) |
| OBS-067-T2-021 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Gal 5:22 | Yes — three axes of operational variation are evidenced. (1) Subject: goodness operates differently when God is subject (ontological-creative, covenantal, dispositional) vs human subject (moral-character, volitional, experiential). (2) Direction: when goodness operates God→human (divine generosity, covenantal promise, chrēstotēs) it is initiatory and enabling; when it operates human→God (praise, trust, walking with God) it is responsive; when it operates human→human (kindness, justice, instruction) it is expressive. (3) Constitutional level: agathōsunē (885-001, Volition/04) operates at the level of resolve and Spirit-enabled virtue; chrēstotēs (886-002, Moral Character/05) operates at the level of settled relational disposition; H2896A in 884-003 operates at the experiential-orientation level. The operational differences map to the 12 modes but cluster into these three axes. (OBS-067-OBS-016, OBS-067-OBS-017, OBS-067-OBS-048) |
| OBS-067-T2-025 | VERSE_PATTERN | Rom 15:14, 2Th 1:11 | The sustained effects named in the verse evidence: (1) Stable inner orientation rooted in nearness to God — Psa 73:28: Asaph's crisis of doubt resolved into a permanently reoriented inner life ("it is good to be near God"). This is not a momentary feeling but a repositioned inner orientation. (2) Community-building capacity — Rom 15:14: persons "full of goodness" are "able to instruct one another" — sustained goodness produces the capacity to contribute to the formation of others. (3) Settled dispositional kindness toward others — Col 3:12: chrēstotēs as "garment" of the renewed person — a sustained character quality, not an occasional kindness. (4) Completed righteous resolve — 2Th 1:11: God's sustained work fulfils "every resolve for good" — over time, the person's Spirit-enabled goodness is completed toward its intended expression. (OBS-067-OBS-029, OBS-067-OBS-040, SBF-067-Q039) |
| OBS-067-T2-026 | VERSE_PATTERN | Rom 15:14 | States established: inner stability (Psa 73:28 — the condition of being near God as stable reference point); gladness rooted in God (contrast with Haman's fragile gladness, Est 5:9 vs the God-rooted condition of 884-003). Qualities established: moral assessiveness — the capacity to recognise what is and is not good (884-004, 884-006); relational generosity — the settled disposition to act with kindness (886-002, Col 3:12). Capacities established: instruction of others (Rom 15:14); doing justice and loving kindness (Mic 6:8); completion of resolve for good (2Th 1:11). Orientations established: toward God as the primary reference for the good (Psa 73:28); toward community as the natural overflow of Spirit-filled goodness (Rom 15:14). | OBS-067-T2-027 | VERSE_PATTERN | 2Th 1:11 | Yes — there is a clear distinction. The immediate response to encountering divine goodness is trust/refuge (Psa 34:8) and praise (doxological group). The sustained effect is repositioned inner orientation (Psa 73:28) and community capacity (Rom 15:14). The immediate response is reactive — a first movement of the inner being toward the good encountered. The sustained effect is constitutive — a settled state that reshapes the person's character, orientation, and relational capacity over time. The distinction is most sharply drawn in Psa 73 where Asaph's encounter with divine goodness produces a sustained reorientation rather than a momentary response. 2Th 1:11's "fulfil every resolve for good" confirms the sustained/completion dimension — goodness works toward completion, not just initiation. (OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-029, SBF-067-Q031) |
| OBS-067-T2-028 | VERSE_PATTERN | Gal 5:22 | Three enabling inner conditions converge (SBF-067-Q014): (1) Proximity/orientation toward God — Psa 73:28 ("it is good to be near God"). The inner condition of nearness, of having God as one's refuge, enables reception of what is genuinely good. (2) Fear of the Lord — Pro 15:16 ("better is a little with the fear of the Lord"). The inner posture of reverential dependence is the ground of receiving the good. (3) Spirit-filling — Gal 5:22 / Rom 15:14. The Spirit's presence in the inner being produces goodness and enables its reception and expression. These three are not independent conditions — they converge on a single posture: the person oriented toward God, filled by his Spirit, whose inner life has been reoriented toward the source of goodness. Additionally, trust/faith is named as the condition for ongoing experience of divine chrēstotēs (Rom 11:22 — "provided you continue in his kindness"). | OBS-067-T2-032 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Rom 15:14 | For Moral Character (05) as primary human dimension: Mic 6:8 defines human goodness as a tri-fold moral orientation (justice, kindness, humble walk). 884-002 (39 verses) is the largest human-subject group and explicitly names inner moral quality. 884-006 (22 verses) names the negative moral verdict — both groups confirm moral character as the primary register of human goodness in H2896A. | OBS-067-T2-033 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Gal 5:22 | Secondary dimensions confirmed: Cognition (03) — 884-004 (comparative wisdom evaluation) and 884-006 (moral verdict assessment) both require the cognitive evaluation faculty. Volition (04) — 884-008 (volitional preference idiom, 40 verses) and 885-001 (Spirit-produced goodness as resolve, 2Th 1:11). The secondary dimensions do not compete with the primary — they represent the multi-modal nature of the characteristic. Moral Character is primary because it characterises the person's inner being as good; Cognition is secondary because the moral evaluation faculty is engaged in assessing what is good; Volition is secondary because goodness both criteria the will and reconstitutes it. | OBS-067-T2-034 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Gal 5:22 | Spirit-level location is confirmed through the pneumatological framework of the NT evidence. Gal 5:22 names agathōsunē and chrēstotēs as "fruit of the Spirit" — the Spirit is the active producing agent and goodness is the fruit produced. The locus of Spirit-production is the human spirit/inner being. 2 Cor 6:6 lists chrēstotēs alongside "the Holy Spirit" in a single phrase, further linking the characteristic's operation to the Spirit's presence. Rom 15:14 ("full of goodness") implies an infilling — a Spirit-level saturation of the inner being with goodness. The Hebrew side does not use "spirit" language directly for tov but the covenantal-renewal context of Eze 36:31 is followed by Eze 36:26–27 (God's Spirit placed within) — goodness recognised and received is structurally connected in the Ezekiel context to Spirit-indwelling. The spirit-level location is confirmed for NT goodness and implied for the covenantal renewal context. (OBS-067-OBS-008, OBS-067-OBS-016, OBS-067-OBS-025) |
| OBS-067-T2-035 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Gal 5:22 | For Spirit-produced goodness (885-001, 886-002): yes — the Spirit is the originating agent. For the Hebrew H2896A doxological and covenantal groups (884-001, 884-005): the origin is God himself, whose goodness is encountered and received by the human inner being. The characteristic does not originate in the human spirit unaided — in all cases the origin is external to the person (God's character, God's Spirit, God's word). The human spirit/inner being is the site of reception, not generation. This structural finding — that goodness is not self-generated — is consistent across all 12 modes. (OBS-067-OBS-001, OBS-067-OBS-016, OBS-067-OBS-039) |
| OBS-067-T2-036 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Gal 5:22 | Spirit-level location reveals that goodness, in its fullest NT expression, is not a surface behaviour or a cultivated habit — it is a deep constitutional transformation produced at the level where the Spirit operates in the person. The contrast with the fallen condition (Rom 3:12 — complete absence of goodness in the unregenerate inner being) confirms that genuine goodness requires Spirit-level intervention. The NT's pneumatological concentration of goodness (agathōsunē as Pauline coinage, chrēstotēs as Spirit-fruit) signals that the deepest form of goodness is not achieved but infused — it comes from the deepest level of divine engagement with the human inner being. This implies that human attempts to produce goodness without Spirit-engagement will produce the surface form — the Haman problem (Est 5:9) — rather than the genuine article. (OBS-067-OBS-046, OBS-067-OBS-041, OBS-067-OBS-039) |
| OBS-067-T2-041 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Rom 15:14 | Direct mind-location is not explicitly named in the verse evidence. However, the cognitive register of goodness is evidenced through the dimension assignment: 884-004 (comparative wisdom evaluation) and 884-006 (moral verdict) are assigned Cognition (03), indicating that the mind's evaluative and discerning function is engaged. The comparative wisdom idiom ("better than") is a cognitive-evaluative operation — assessing and ranking goods. This is a mind-faculty operation even if the term "mind" is not explicitly used. Rom 15:14 pairs goodness with "all knowledge" in the same clause — "full of goodness, filled with all knowledge" — suggesting that goodness and cognitive knowledge are related inner-being qualities. The evidence locates goodness at the evaluative level of mind-function, but explicit mind-language is absent. (OBS-067-OBS-012, OBS-067-OBS-025) |
| OBS-067-T2-048 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Gal 5:22 | Origin is consistently external to the person — received from God and bestowed through the Spirit. Three origin paths: (1) Divine character as origin — God is good and goodness flows from his character (Psa 119:68; 884-001); (2) Covenantal word as origin — God's good word is spoken and received in the human inner being (Jos 23:14; 884-005); (3) Spirit-production as origin — agathōsunē and chrēstotēs are Spirit-fruit (Gal 5:22; 885-001, 886-002). The key negative evidence: Rom 3:12 names the complete absence of goodness in the unregenerate condition — confirming that goodness is not naturally generated from within. The origin is not generational (no evidence for generational goodness transmission as a constitutional mechanism, though the covenantal promise "to thousands" implies relational continuity). | OBS-067-T2-049 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Gal 5:22 | The origin is formally singular (God as ultimate source) but operationally multiple in its delivery mechanisms. The ultimate origin is God's own goodness — this is singular and consistent. The delivery mechanisms are: God's character encountered (experiential), God's word received (covenantal), God's Spirit infused (pneumatological). These three mechanisms are not competing origins but three modes through which the singular divine source of goodness reaches the human inner being. This is analytically significant: the programme's 12 modes of goodness all trace back to the same originating source (God's goodness) but through different delivery paths. (OBS-067-OBS-001, OBS-067-OBS-008, OBS-067-OBS-016, OBS-067-OBS-039) |
| OBS-067-T2-050 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Gal 5:22 | The ultimate origin (God's goodness) does not change. What changes is the delivery mechanism and the register of goodness received. In the Hebrew experiential register (884-003), the origin reaches the person through encounter and nearness. In the covenantal register (884-005), through God's word and promise-keeping. In the NT pneumatological register (885-001, 886-002), through the Spirit's production. These represent a progressive clarification and concentration of how goodness is delivered — from encounter and word in the OT to Spirit-production in the NT — but the source is constant. What shifts is not the origin but the mechanism of delivery and the specificity of naming. The NT's pneumatological precision is a clarification, not a change of origin. (OBS-067-OBS-016, OBS-067-OBS-099) |
| OBS-067-T2-051 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Gal 5:22 | Constitutional movement is present and traceable. The primary movement is: Spirit-level origin (Spirit-production, Gal 5:22) → soul-level reception and orientation (Lam 3:25; Psa 73:28 — the soul seeks and is satisfied) → heart-level engagement (knowing in hearts, Jos 23:14; glad of heart, Est 5:9) → outward expression in conduct (Mic 6:8 — doing justice; Rom 15:14 — instructing others). This is a top-down and outward movement: from the Spirit's action in the innermost level, through the soul's orientation and the heart's response, to visible conduct and community expression. The inverse movement (body feeding back to soul) is not strongly evidenced for goodness. The constitutional movement is consistently inward-to-outward. (OBS-067-OBS-016, OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-039) |
| OBS-067-T2-052 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Gal 5:22, 2Th 1:11 | The sequence is: (1) Divine source acts (God's goodness, Spirit's production, God's word) → (2) Spirit-level reception in the inner being (Spirit-fruit, infilling with goodness) → (3) Soul reorientation (Psa 73:28 — repositioned toward God; Lam 3:25 — the soul seeking) → (4) Heart engagement (knowing, gladness, moral recognition) → (5) Volitional alignment (choosing good, willing submission, Jer 26:14) → (6) Outward expression (conduct, justice, instruction of others). This is a formation sequence, not an instantaneous transformation. The 2Th 1:11 language ("fulfil every resolve for good") implies that step 5 (volitional resolve) is followed by step 6 (completion by God's power) — the full sequence requires both human resolve and divine completion. (OBS-067-OBS-016, OBS-067-OBS-039, OBS-067-OBS-040, SBF-067-Q031) |
| OBS-067-T2-057 | VERSE_PATTERN | Rom 15:14 | Goodness enables and deepens cognition. Rom 15:14 pairs goodness with knowledge in a single characterological portrait: "full of goodness, filled with all knowledge" — suggesting a natural coherence between goodness and cognitive fullness. The absence of goodness impairs cognition: the moral inversion of Mal 2:17 / Jer 44:17 (calling evil good) is a cognitive failure — the evaluative faculty is corrupted. The direction is clear: goodness present deepens moral cognition; goodness absent or distorted impairs it. (OBS-067-OBS-012, OBS-067-OBS-021, OBS-067-OBS-025) |
| OBS-067-T2-058 | VERSE_PATTERN | Rom 15:14 | The cognitive engagement reveals that goodness is not ethically naive or merely affective — it requires intellectual content. The wisdom literature's comparative evaluations demand a capacity for moral reasoning. The pairing of goodness with knowledge (Rom 15:14) suggests that genuine goodness has a cognitive substrate — the person who is good knows what is good and why. This is consistent with the Mic 6:8 revelatory frame ("He has told you what is good") — goodness is disclosed knowledge, not merely felt impulse. The pattern further reveals that goodness in its distorted form (calling evil good) specifically corrupts the cognitive faculty — which implies that genuine goodness and genuine cognition are structurally coherent. | OBS-067-T2-065 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | 2Th 1:11, Gal 5:22 | Yes — Volition (04) is a confirmed secondary dimension. Goodness engages volition both as the criterion (what the will should choose) and as the reconstituted capacity (Spirit-enabled resolve toward goodness). | OBS-067-T2-066 | VERSE_PATTERN | 2Th 1:11 | Goodness reconstitutes volition rather than bypassing or overriding it. 2Th 1:11 makes this precise: "may God fulfil every resolve for good" — the human resolve is real and operative; God's power fulfils it (does not replace it). The structure is: Spirit-produced goodness produces a genuine resolve in the human will → God's power fulfils that resolve → the human agent acts. The will's capacity is enabled (Spirit-production enables the resolve), the will's interaction with other characteristics is shaped (goodness reconstitutes what the will chooses as its object), and the will operates under the constraint of the good as revealed (Mic 6:8 — "He has told you what is good" sets the constraint within which the will's proper operation is defined). Volition without this reconstitution produces self-direction (Isa 65:2) or wilful refusal (Jer 6:16) — the will's natural operation in the fallen condition is away from the good. (OBS-067-OBS-014, OBS-067-OBS-039, OBS-067-OBS-040, SBF-067-Q040) |
| OBS-067-T2-067 | VERSE_PATTERN | 2Th 1:11 | The volitional engagement reveals that goodness is not merely a character quality but an active principle that must be chosen and willed. Goodness does not produce compliance or passive absorption — it produces resolve ("every resolve for good," 2Th 1:11) and active choosing ("do what seems good," 884-008). The person who possesses goodness chooses it actively — Col 3:12 frames this as "put on therefore" — a deliberate volitional act enabled by prior transformation. This reveals that goodness has a volitional depth that distinguishes it from passive character states: it is both a quality possessed and a quality actively willed. The reconstitution of volition by goodness means that the good person is not merely compliant but genuinely desirous of the good — the will itself has been reoriented rather than overridden. (OBS-067-OBS-039, OBS-067-OBS-040, SBF-067-Q040) |
| OBS-067-T2-068 | VERSE_PATTERN | 2Th 1:11 | Agency is engaged and required. Mic 6:8 requires active human doing — "to do justice, and to love kindness, and to walk humbly." The goodness defined here is not a state but a practice — it requires the person to initiate and sustain action. The "garment" language of Col 3:12 ("put on therefore... kindness") frames goodness as an active choice to take up — an agentive act. Pro 16:32 ("he who rules his spirit than he who takes a city") names self-governance as an agency act with positive moral value. 2Th 1:11's "every resolve for good" is a person's own resolve — the agentive capacity is intact and engaged. Goodness does not bypass agency; it requires it and enables it. (OBS-067-OBS-027, OBS-067-OBS-040, SBF-067-Q040) |

This is not a reduction of agency but an amplification of it — the Spirit-enabled person has a deeper capacity for agentive goodness than the unregenerate person (whose agency is misdirected toward self-direction, Isa 65:2). Col 3:12's "put on" is an agency act — the Spirit's prior transformation is the enabling ground, and the human agentive choice is the expression. Goodness also provides the criterion for agency's proper exercise (Mic 6:8 — doing justice and loving kindness require active choosing and doing). The deepening of agency through goodness confirms that genuine goodness is not quietist or passive — it is an inner quality that demands expression. The contrast with the fallen condition (Rom 3:12: "no one does good, not even one" — agency directed away from the good) confirms that the agency-restoration produced by goodness is a constitutive element of the characteristic's full expression. | OBS-067-T2-077 | VERSE_PATTERN | 2Th 1:11 | Conscientiousness is the integrating faculty that brings together moral awareness, will, and action — and goodness is one of the most comprehensively integrated characteristics in the programme precisely at this level. | OBS-067-T2-080 | VERSE_PATTERN | Rom 15:14 | Yes — relational capacity is extensively engaged. The inner quality expressed through chrēstotēs is the disposition to act with goodness toward another — a relational orientation by definition. Mic 6:8 frames goodness as relational in its human expression: doing justice (right action toward others), loving kindness (relational affection and loyalty), walking with God (vertical relational orientation) — all three are relational in direction. Rom 15:14 confirms: goodness-filled persons are "able to instruct one another" — relational capacity as an expression of goodness. | OBS-067-T2-081 | VERSE_PATTERN | Rom 15:14 | Goodness enables and deepens relational capacity. The Spirit-produced chrēstotēs (886-002) is itself a relational capacity — it is the inner disposition enabling generous engagement toward others. Rom 15:14's "able to instruct one another" names a relational capacity (mutual edification) produced by goodness. The giving of goodness toward others (Col 3:12 — put on kindness; Mic 6:8 — love kindness and do justice) requires and develops relational capacity. The Haman instance (Est 5:9) shows how goodness-without-root produces a fragile inner state that makes genuine relational goodness toward others unstable. | OBS-067-T2-082 | VERSE_PATTERN | Rom 15:14 | The relational engagement pattern reveals that goodness in its full expression is essentially outward-directed. The characteristic builds relational capacity in two directions simultaneously: toward God (vertical — walking with God, seeking God, receiving his goodness) and toward others (horizontal — justice, kindness, instruction, community). This dual-directional relational engagement is structurally coherent with the Mic 6:8 definition: the tri-fold good involves both the vertical (walking humbly with God) and the horizontal (doing justice, loving kindness). The relational pattern further reveals that goodness is a characteristic that naturally overflows from the inner being toward others — the person "full of goodness" (Rom 15:14) becomes a relational resource for the community. Goodness therefore builds rather than merely sustains relational connection — it generates new relational capacities in the one who possesses it. (OBS-067-OBS-017, OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-027) |
| OBS-067-T2-083 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Gal 5:22 | God-to-human operation is one of the best-evidenced dimensions of goodness across the whole registry. Four distinct modes: (1) Character declaration — God declares himself good and his goodness toward his people (Psa 119:68; 884-001 doxological group). The declaration is itself an act of divine goodness toward the human — it names what the human may trust. (2) Covenantal word and promise — 884-005 (17 verses, anchor Jos 23:14): God's good word given and kept is goodness operating from God toward the people through promise and faithfulness. (3) Creative provision — Gen 1:31 (884-007): God's pronouncement of creation as good is the foundational act of goodness-toward-creation. (4) Pneumatological gift — Gal 5:22 / Rom 15:14: the Spirit produces goodness in the believer — goodness flows from God to the human through the Spirit's infilling. (5) Chrēstotēs as divine disposition — Rom 11:22; Eph 2:7: God's generous goodwill toward humanity is named explicitly and described as displayed supremely in Christ. (OBS-067-OBS-006, OBS-067-OBS-016, OBS-067-OBS-034, SBF-067-Q006) |
| OBS-067-T2-089 | VERSE_PATTERN | Rom 15:14 | Human-to-human giving of goodness is evidenced in four forms: (1) Instruction and edification — Rom 15:14 ("full of goodness... able to instruct one another"): the goodness-filled person extends goodness toward others through teaching and building up. (2) Kindness as relational disposition — Col 3:12 (put on chrēstotēs as garment): the deliberate expression of generosity of spirit toward others in the community. (3) Justice and right action — Mic 6:8 ("to do justice"): goodness extended toward others as the active practice of just treatment. (4) Covenantal kindness — the tov vocabulary in its relational register covers loyalty and steadfast faithfulness in human relationships, paralleling the divine hesed-goodness pattern. Each of these is an extension of inner goodness toward another person. (OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-027, OBS-067-OBS-039, SBF-067-Q039) |
| OBS-067-T2-090 | VERSE_PATTERN | Rom 15:14, Gal 5:22 | Three enabling inner conditions for giving goodness (SBF-067-Q039): (1) Prior Spirit-transformation — Rom 15:14's community goodness is a Spirit-enabled capacity. Col 3:12's "put on" is explicitly grounded in prior identity transformation ("God's chosen ones, holy and beloved") — the giver must first have received a transformation before they can genuinely give. (2) Encounter with and reception of divine goodness — Psa 73:28's inner reorientation produces the overflow toward others in Psa 73's conclusion (telling of God's works). The person who has genuinely encountered divine goodness has a source of goodness to extend. (3) Spirit-filling — Gal 5:22 / Rom 15:14: the Spirit-produced chrēstotēs and agathōsunē are inner capacities the Spirit supplies. Without Spirit-filling, the person lacks the genuine internal resource for extending goodness. Source is transformation; discipline may shape expression but cannot generate the capacity. (OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-039, SBF-067-Q039) |
| OBS-067-T2-092 | VERSE_PATTERN | Rom 15:14 | Human-from-human receiving of goodness is less directly evidenced than the divine-to-human direction, but is present. Col 3:12 names the community context where chrēstotēs is expressed and received — the "one another" frame of Rom 15:14 implies both giving and receiving. The Mic 6:8 framework implies a community in which justice and kindness are both given and received — the person who does justice and loves kindness creates a relational environment in which others receive goodness. The most explicit receiving is from God — the covenantal reception (Jos 23:14: "you know in your hearts and souls"), the Spirit-reception (Gal 5:22), the encounter reception (Psa 34:8). Human-from-human receiving is implied by the community structure but not directly named in individual anchor verses. (OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-027, SBF-067-Q004) |
| OBS-067-T2-095 | VERSE_PATTERN | Rom 15:14 | The Col 3:12 context places chrēstotēs within the covenant community — the garment metaphor implies a sustained relational environment (the body of Christ) where goodness is the ongoing character of the relational field. Rom 15:14 is similarly community-internal ("my brothers"). These instances suggest that goodness in its NT expression operates primarily within existing relational bonds. However, the Hebrew H2896A in 884-002 and Mic 6:8 does not restrict to existing bonds — "doing justice" and "loving kindness" in Mic 6:8 have an implicitly universal scope in prophetic ethics. The data does not directly contrast in-bond vs cross-boundary operation. This is a genuine partial gap — the NT evidence suggests community-internal; the prophetic evidence implies universal scope. Whether goodness operates differently across these contexts is not directly addressed. (OBS-067-OBS-027, OBS-067-OBS-017) |
| OBS-067-T2-099 | VERSE_PATTERN | Gal 5:22 | Both forms of transformation are present and distinguishable (SBF-067-Q031). (1) Orientation change — Psa 73:28: Asaph's inner life transformed not by changed external circumstances but by a shift in what he orients toward. "It is good to be near God" is the repositioned orientation — his condition (circumstances, opponents) has not changed but his inner orientation has. (2) Character transformation — Spirit-production (Gal 5:22; Rom 15:14): the Spirit changes the inner character itself, not merely its orientation. The person "full of goodness" (Rom 15:14) has undergone a character-level transformation — goodness as an inner quality has been established. (3) Moral awareness transformation — Eze 36:31: the movement from not seeing deeds as not-good to recognising and loathing them is a condition change — from moral blindness to moral sight. This is a change of inner state (the perceptual-moral condition) that precedes orientation change. All three transformation forms are present. (OBS-067-OBS-029, OBS-067-OBS-035, OBS-067-OBS-039, SBF-067-Q031) |
| OBS-067-T2-103 | VERSE_PATTERN | Gal 5:22 | Three distinct mechanisms are evidenced, corresponding to the three transformation types identified at Q&A-123: (1) Encounter mechanism — Psa 34:8 / Psa 73:28: the mechanism is perceptual encounter with divine goodness. The change is produced by tasting and seeing — a direct experiential contact that reorients the inner being. This is neither discipline nor gradual formation but encounter-transformation. (2) Spirit-infusion mechanism — Gal 5:22 / Rom 15:14: the Spirit fills the person with goodness. The mechanism is pneumatological infusion — goodness as fruit is the Spirit's work in the inner being. This is not achieved by effort but received as Spirit-gift. (3) Recognition-confrontation mechanism — Eze 36:31 / Rom 2:4: the mechanism is confrontation with one's own not-goodness in the presence of the divine goodness standard. Memory + recognition + loathing = the mechanism of moral transformation toward goodness. All three mechanisms are present; they are not competing but operate in different registers and at different moments. (OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-035, OBS-067-OBS-039, SBF-067-Q031) |
| OBS-067-T2-104 | VERSE_PATTERN | Gal 5:22 | Yes — the mechanisms are context-differentiated. The encounter mechanism operates in experiential and worship contexts (Psalms — crisis, praise, seeking). The Spirit-infusion mechanism operates in the pneumatological-community context (NT epistolary — Gal, Eph, Rom, Col). The recognition-confrontation mechanism operates in prophetic and apostolic contexts that address moral failure (Eze, Lam, Rom 2). The differentiation is not random — each mechanism is appropriate to its context: the seeking soul receives through encounter; the redeemed community receives through Spirit; the morally blind person is reached through recognition-confrontation. The mechanisms together cover the full range of contexts in which goodness produces transformation. (OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-035, OBS-067-OBS-039) |
| OBS-067-T2-107 | VERSE_PATTERN | Gal 5:22, 2Th 1:11 | Yes — the formation arc is evidenced in the NT evidence. Col 3:12–14 places the "putting on" of chrēstotēs within a longer paraenetic arc: the person has already received new identity transformation ("God's chosen ones, holy and beloved"); is now to clothe themselves with the character qualities that express this identity (3:12); culminating in love that binds everything together in perfect harmony (3:14). This is a formation sequence — the Spirit's prior work, the intentional character-expression, and the sustained orientation toward love as the integrating whole. Gal 5:22–23 similarly places goodness within the fruit of the Spirit — a cluster of nine character qualities that are the full expression of Spirit-formed character. The "fruit" metaphor implies organic growth over time — formation, not instantaneous achievement. (OBS-067-OBS-017, OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-039) |
| OBS-067-T2-108 | VERSE_PATTERN | Gal 5:22, Rom 15:14 | Goodness plays a dual role in the formation arc: (1) As a formation product — goodness is the result of the Spirit's sanctifying work in the person. It is formed in the person through encounter, Spirit-infusion, and sustained character development (Gal 5:22; Col 3:12). In this sense goodness is the goal of formation — what a Spirit-transformed person becomes. (2) As a formation agent — goodness in the person contributes to the formation of others. Rom 15:14 names persons "full of goodness" as those "able to instruct one another" — goodness enables the person to participate in the formation of the community. The good person becomes a formative resource for others. This dual role — goodness as formation product and formation agent — is a distinctive structural finding for this characteristic. (OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-039, SBF-067-Q039) |
| OBS-067-T2-109 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | 2Th 1:11 | Partial eschatological evidence is present. Eph 2:7 ("so that in the coming ages he might show the immeasurable riches of his grace in kindness toward us in Christ Jesus") explicitly places chrēstotēs in a future-oriented eschatological frame — God's chrēstotēs will be displayed in its fullness in the coming ages. This names an eschatological trajectory: present experience of divine kindness anticipates its future unrestricted display. 2Th 1:11 ("fulfil every resolve for good") implies a completion — God's completing act brings present goodness-resolve to its fullness. However, the specifically eschatological texture of goodness (what it will be in the new creation, what fullness means) is not directly described in the anchor verses beyond these two instances. The trajectory is indicated but not fully developed. (OBS-067-OBS-008, OBS-067-OBS-016, SBF-067-Q006) |
| OBS-067-T2-110 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | 2Th 1:11 | Eph 2:7 implies that present experience of chrēstotēs is a foretaste of the "immeasurable riches" of its future expression — present goodness is real but partial relative to its coming fullness. The "immeasurable" qualifier suggests that the eschatological form of goodness exceeds present experience in scale and richness. 2Th 1:11's "fulfil every resolve for good" implies that present resolves for goodness, even when genuine, are not yet complete — their completion is a divine eschatological act. The present experience of goodness therefore anticipates: (1) A fullness of divine kindness-display that surpasses present experience; (2) A completion of human goodness-resolve that requires divine power to finish. The gap is that the data does not describe what the experiential content of eschatological goodness will be — only that it will be fuller and completed. (OBS-067-OBS-008, OBS-067-OBS-016) |

| OBS-067-T2-113 | CROSS_REGISTRY | 2Th 1:11 | Two sequential relationships are directly named: (1) Goodness → repentance (Rom 2:4): "God's kindness is meant to lead you to repentance" — chrēstotēs explicitly precedes and produces repentance. The sequence is causal: divine goodness is prior, repentance follows. (2) Goodness → faith/trust (Psa 34:8): encounter with divine goodness ("taste and see that the Lord is good") is followed by "blessed is the man who takes refuge in him" — goodness is the experiential prior that produces the faith/refuge response. Goodness precedes faith in the encounter sequence. A third sequence is implied by SBF-067-Q133 (prior analysis): goodness is prior to faith (encounter with goodness → faith response); 2Th 1:11 shows them as parallel co-products in the other direction. These sequential findings are confirmed and structured. (OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-043, SBF-067-Q127, SBF-067-Q133) |
| OBS-067-T2-114 | CROSS_REGISTRY | 2Th 1:11 | The goodness → repentance sequence (Rom 2:4) is explicitly causal: "is meant to lead to" — divine chrēstotēs is the mechanism producing repentance. The goodness → faith sequence (Psa 34:8) is causal-enabling: the experiential encounter with goodness enables and produces the trust response. The goodness-and-faith parallel sequence (2Th 1:11: "every resolve for good and every work of faith") is correlational — they are co-produced by God's power rather than one causing the other. The three sequential relationships reveal three different structural relationships: causal (goodness produces repentance), enabling-causal (goodness enables faith-response), and correlational (goodness-resolve and faith-work as parallel Spirit-expressions). (OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-043, SBF-067-Q127) |

The Spirit is the enabling cause of agathōsunē and chrēstotēs as inner qualities of the believer. On this reading, goodness in its human expression is not a simple quality but is constituted by these three orientations together. | OBS-067-T2-120 | ROOT_FINDING | Gal 5:22 | The TOV root sharing between R67 and R103 reveals the closest conceptual relationship in the programme — goodness and love share a root at the most fundamental lexical level. The Hebrew does not cleanly separate them: the same root family generates both the quality of goodness (H2896A) and the relational pleasure/love vocabulary (H2895, H2898). This lexical proximity implies a conceptual proximity: Hebrew goodness and Hebrew love are not adjacent but overlapping at the root. The AGATHO root sharing between R67 and R65 reveals the programme's structural decision to separate inner disposition (agathōsunē, R67) from outward action (agathopoieo, R65) — a distinction that is real but is not native to the Hebrew H2896A, which serves both registers. The root sharing reveals that the programme's registry boundaries are analytical decisions made against a vocabulary that does not share those boundaries. Session D must reckon with this. (OBS-067-OBS-018, OBS-067-OBS-090, SP-067-001, SP-067-011) |
| OBS-067-T2-121 | CROSS_REGISTRY | Gal 5:22 | Three closest neighbours are identifiable: (1) R103 (love) — shares root vocabulary at the deepest level (H2895, H2898 in R103; H2896A in R67). The distinction between goodness (R67) and kindness (R99) at the level of chrēstotēs is analytically unresolved — the boundary is the programme's assignment decision. (3) R065 (generosity) — shares the agatho root. Goodness (R67) is the inner quality; generosity (R65) is the active doing of good. The distinction is inner disposition vs outward act. The precise boundaries for (1) and (2) are not fully drawn in the current data — Session D territory. (OBS-067-OBS-018, OBS-067-OBS-090, SP-067-001, SP-067-011) |
